language governing permissions and\\n16:  * limitations under the License.\\n17:  */\\n18: \\n19: package org.apache.flink.api.connector.source;\\n20: \\n21: import org.apache.flink.annotation.Public;\\n22: import org.apache.flink.annotation.PublicEvolving;\\n23: import org.apache.flink.api.common.state.CheckpointListener;\\n24: import org.apache.flink.core.io.InputStatus;\\n25: import org.apache.flink.metrics.Gauge;\\n26: import org.apache.flink.metrics.groups.OperatorIOMetricGroup;\\n27: import org.apache.flink.metrics.groups.SourceReaderMetricGroup;\\n28: \\n29: import java.util.Collection;\\n30: import java.util.List;\\n31: import java.util.concurrent.CompletableFuture;\\n32: \\n33: /**\\n34:  * The interface for a source reader which is responsible for reading the records from the source\\n35:  * splits assigned by {@link SplitEnumerator}.\\n36:  *\\n37:  * <p>For most non-trivial source reader, it is recommended to use {@link\\n38:  * org.apache.flink.connector.base.source.reader.SourceReaderBase SourceReaderBase} which provides\\n39:  * an efficient hand-over protocol to avoid blocking I/O inside the task thread and supports various\\n40:  * split-threading models.\\n41:  *\\n42:  * <p>Implementations can provide the following metrics:\\n43:  *\\n44:  * <ul>\\n45:  *   <li>{@link OperatorIOMetricGroup#getNumRecordsInCounter()} (highly recommended)\\n46:  *   <li>{@link OperatorIOMetricGroup#getNumBytesInCounter()} (recommended)\\n47:  *   <li>{@link SourceReaderMetricGroup#getNumRecordsInErrorsCounter()} (recommended)\\n48:  *   <li>{@link SourceReaderMetricGroup#setPendingRecordsGauge(Gauge)}\\n49:  *   <li>{@link SourceReaderMetricGroup#setPendingBytesGauge(Gauge)}\\n50:  * </ul>\\n51:  *\\n52:  * @param <T> The type of the record emitted by this source reader.\\n53:  * @param <SplitT> The type of the source splits.\\n54:  */\\n55: @Public\\n56: public interface SourceReader<T, SplitT extends SourceSplit>\\n57:         extends AutoCloseable, CheckpointListener {\\n58: \\n59:     /** Start the reader. */\\n60:     void start();\\n61: \\n62:     /**\\n63:      * Poll the next available record into the {@link ReaderOutput}.\\n64:      *\\n65:      * <p>The implementation must make sure this method is non-blocking.\\n66:      *\\n67:      * <p>Although the implementation can emit multiple records into the given ReaderOutput, it is\\n68:      * recommended not doing so. Instead, emit one record into the ReaderOutput and return a {@link\\n69:      * InputStatus#MORE_AVAILABLE} to let the caller thread know there are more records available.\\n70:      *\\n71:      * @return The InputStatus of the SourceReader after the method invocation.\\n72:      */\\n73:     InputStatus pollNext(ReaderOutput<T> output) throws Exception;\\n74: \\n75:     /**\\n76:      * Checkpoint on the state of the source.\\n77:      *\\n78:      * @return the state of the source.\\n79:      */\\n80:     List<SplitT> snapshotState(long checkpointId);\\n81: \\n82:     /**\\n83:      * Returns a future that signals that data is available from the reader.\\n84:      *\\n85:      * <p>Once the future completes, the runtime will keep calling the {@link\\n86:      * #pollNext(ReaderOutput)} method until that method returns a status other than {@link\\n87:      * InputStatus#MORE_AVAILABLE}. After that, the runtime will again call this method to obtain\\n88:      * the next future. Once that completes, it will again call {@link #pollNext(ReaderOutput)} and\\n89:      * so on.\\n90:      *\\n91:      * <p>The contract is the following: If the reader has data available, then all futures\\n92:      * previously returned by this method must eventually complete. Otherwise the source might stall\\n93:      * indefinitely.\\n94:      *\\n95:      * <p>It is not a problem to have occasional \\\"false positives\\\", meaning to complete a future\\n96:      * even if no data is available. However, one should not use an \\\"always complete\\\" future in\\n97:      * cases no data is available, because that will result in busy waiting loops calling {@code\\n98:      * pollNext(...)} even though no data is available.\\n99:      *\\n100:      * @return a future that will be completed once there is a record available to poll.\\n101:      */\\n102:     CompletableFuture<Void> isAvailable();\\n103: \\n104:     /**\\n105:      * Adds a list of splits for this reader to read. The fetch call could be blocking\\n40:      * but it should get unblocked when {@link #wakeUp()} is invoked. In that case, the\\n41:      * implementation may either decide to return without throwing an exception, or it can just\\n42:      * throw an interrupted exception. In either case, this method should be reentrant, meaning that\\n43:      * the next fetch call should just resume from where the last fetch call was waken up or\\n44:      * interrupted. It is up to the implementer to either read all the records of the split or to\\n45:      * stop reading them at some point (for example when a given threshold is exceeded). In that\\n46:      * later case, when fetch is called again, the reading should restart at the record where it\\n47:      * left off based on the {@code SplitState}.\\n48:      *\\n49:      * @return the Ids of the finished splits.\\n50:      * @throws IOException when encountered IO errors, such as deserialization failures.\\n51:      */\\n52:     RecordsWithSplitIds<E> fetch() throws IOException;\\n53: \\n54:     /**\\n55:      * Handle the split changes. This call should be non-blocking.\\n56:      *\\n57:      * <p>For the consistency of internal state in SourceReaderBase, if an invalid split is added to\\n58:      * the reader (for example splits without any records), it should be put back into {@link\\n59:      * RecordsWithSplitIds} as finished splits so that SourceReaderBase could be able to clean up\\n60:      * resources created for it.\\n61:      *\\n62:      * <p>For the consistency of internal state in SourceReaderBase, if a split is removed, it\\n63:      * should be put back into {@link RecordsWithSplitIds} as finished splits so that\\n64:      * SourceReaderBase could be able to clean up resources created for it.\\n65:      *\\n66:      * @param splitsChanges the split changes that the SplitReader needs to handle.\\n67:      */\\n68:     void handleSplitsChanges(SplitsChange<SplitT> splitsChanges);\\n69: \\n70:     /** Wake up the split reader in case the fetcher thread is blocking in {@link #fetch()}. */\\n71:     void wakeUp();\\n72: \\n73:     /**\\n74:      * Pauses or resumes reading of individual splits readers.\\n75:      *\\n76:      * <p>Note that no other methods can be called in parallel, so it's fine to non-atomically\\n77:      * update subscriptions. This method is simply providing connectors with more expressive APIs\\n78:      * the opportunity to update all subscriptions at once.\\n79:      *\\n80:      * <p>This is currently used to align the watermarks of splits, if watermark alignment is used\\n81:      * and the source reads from more than one split.\\n82:      *\\n83:      * <p>The default implementation throws an {@link UnsupportedOperationException} where the\\n84:      * default implementation will be removed in future releases. To be compatible with future\\n85:      * releases, it is recommended to implement this method and override the default implementation.\\n86:      *\\n87:      * @param splitsToPause the splits to pause\\n88:      * @param splitsToResume the splits to resume\\n89:      */\\n90:     default void pauseOrResumeSplits(\\n91:             Collection<SplitT> splitsToPause, Collection<SplitT> splitsToResume) {\\n92:         throw new UnsupportedOperationException(\\n93:                 \\\"This split reader does not support pausing or resuming splits which can lead to unaligned splits.\\\\n\\\"\\n94:                         + \\\"Unaligned splits are splits where the output watermarks of the splits have diverged more than the allowed limit.\\\\n\\\"\\n95:                         + \\\"It is highly discouraged to use unaligned source splits, as this leads to unpredictable\\\\n\\\"\\n96:                         + \\\"watermark alignment if there is more than a single split per reader. It is recommended to implement pausing splits\\\\n\\\"\\n97:                         + \\\"for this source. At your own risk, you can allow unaligned source splits by setting the\\\\n\\\"\\n98:                         + \\\"configuration parameter `pipeline.watermark-alignment.allow-unaligned-source-splits' to true.\\\\n\\\"\\n99:                         + \\\"Beware that this configuration parameter will be dropped in a future Flink release.\\\");\\n100:     }\\n101: }\\n102: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/flink--0cc95fcc@de39c3e1777c43fe3363b3fd7784bf46b57a99c2/-/blob/flink-connectors/flink-connector-base/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/connector/base/source/reader/splitreader/SplitReader.java\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"f88f8b8d-c080-4510-a5ce-bae3838faaef","uuid":"4e9c3272-ffc7-48f1-ad0e-ec6a49120ddb","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2:  * Licensed to the Apache Software Foundation (ASF) under one\\n3:  * or more contributor license agreements. It is up to the implementer to either read all the records of the split or to\\n45:      * stop reading them at some point (for example when a given threshold is exceeded). In that\\n46:      * later case, when fetch is called again, the reading should restart at the record where it\\n47:      * left off based on the {@code SplitState}.\\n48:      *\\n49:      * @return the Ids of the finished splits.\\n50:      * @throws IOException when encountered IO errors, such as deserialization failures.\\n51:      */\\n52:     RecordsWithSplitIds<E> fetch() throws IOException;\\n53: \\n54:     /**\\n55:      * Handle the split changes. This call should be non-blocking.\\n56:      *\\n57:      * <p>For the consistency of internal state in SourceReaderBase, if an invalid split is added to\\n58:      * the reader (for example splits without any records), it should be put back into {@link\\n59:      * RecordsWithSplitIds} as finished splits so that SourceReaderBase could be able to clean up\\n60:      * resources created for it.\\n61:      *\\n62:      * <p>For the consistency of internal state in SourceReaderBase, if a split is removed, it\\n63:      * should be put back into {@link RecordsWithSplitIds} as finished splits so that\\n64:      * SourceReaderBase could be able to clean up resources created for it.\\n65:      *\\n66:      * @param splitsChanges the split changes that the SplitReader needs to handle.\\n67:      */\\n68:     void handleSplitsChanges(SplitsChange<SplitT> splitsChanges);\\n69: \\n70:     /** Wake up the split reader in case the fetcher thread is blocking in {@link #fetch()}. */\\n71:     void wakeUp();\\n72: \\n73:     /**\\n74:      * Pauses or resumes reading of individual splits readers.\\n75:      *\\n76:      * <p>Note that no other methods can be called in parallel, so it's fine to non-atomically\\n77:      * update subscriptions. This method is simply providing connectors with more expressive APIs\\n78:      * the opportunity to update all subscriptions at once.\\n79:      *\\n80:      * <p>This is currently used to align the watermarks of splits, if watermark alignment is used\\n81:      * and the source reads from more than one split.\\n82:      *\\n83:      * <p>The default implementation throws an {@link UnsupportedOperationException} where the\\n84:      * default implementation will be removed in future releases. To be compatible with future\\n85:      * releases, it is recommended to implement this method and override the default implementation.\\n86:      *\\n87:      * @param splitsToPause the splits to pause\\n88:      * @param splitsToResume the splits to resume\\n89:      */\\n90:     default void pauseOrResumeSplits(\\n91:             Collection<SplitT> splitsToPause, Collection<SplitT> splitsToResume) {\\n92:         throw new UnsupportedOperationException(\\n93:                 \\\"This split reader does not support pausing or resuming splits which can lead to unaligned splits.\\\\n\\\"\\n94:                         + \\\"Unaligned splits are splits where the output watermarks of the splits have diverged more than the allowed limit.\\\\n\\\"\\n95:                         + \\\"It is highly discouraged to use unaligned source splits, as this leads to unpredictable\\\\n\\\"\\n96:                         + \\\"watermark alignment if there is more than a single split per reader. It is recommended to implement pausing splits\\\\n\\\"\\n97:                         + \\\"for this source. At your own risk, you can allow unaligned source splits by setting the\\\\n\\\"\\n98:                         + \\\"configuration parameter `pipeline.watermark-alignment.allow-unaligned-source-splits' to true.\\\\n\\\"\\n99:                         + \\\"Beware that this configuration parameter will be dropped in a future Flink release.\\\");\\n100:     }\\n101: }\\n102: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/flink--0cc95fcc@de39c3e1777c43fe3363b3fd7784bf46b57a99c2/-/blob/flink-connectors/flink-connector-base/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/connector/base/source/reader/splitreader/SplitReader.java\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"1: /*\n2:  * Licensed to the Apache Software Foundation (ASF) under one\n3:  * or more contributor license agreements.  See the NOTICE file\n4:  * distributed with this work for additional information\n5:  * regarding copyright ownership.  The ASF licenses this file\n6:  * to you under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the\n7:  * \"License\"); you may not use this file except in compliance\n8:  * with the License.  You may obtain a copy of the License at\n9:  *\n10:  *     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n11:  *\n12:  * Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n13:  * distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n14:  * WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n15:  * See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n16:  * limitations under the License.\n17:  */\n18: \n19: package org.apache.flink.connector.base.source.reader.splitreader;\n20: \n21: import org.apache.flink.annotation.PublicEvolving;\n22: import org.apache.flink.api.connector.source.SourceSplit;\n23: import org.apache.flink.connector.base.source.reader.RecordsWithSplitIds;\n24: \n25: import java.io.IOException;\n26: import java.util.Collection;\n27: \n28: /**\n29:  * An interface used to read from splits. The implementation could either read from a single split\n30:  * or from multiple splits.\n31:  *\n32:  * @param <E> the element type.\n33:  * @param <SplitT> the split type.\n34:  */\n35: @PublicEvolving\n36: public interface SplitReader<E, SplitT extends SourceSplit> extends AutoCloseable {\n37: \n38:     /**\n39:      * Fetch elements into the blocking queue for the given splits. The fetch call could be blocking\n40:      * but it should get unblocked when {@link #wakeUp()} is invoked. In that case, the\n41:      * implementation may either decide to return without throwing an exception, or it can just\n42:      * throw an interrupted exception. In either case, this method should be reentrant, meaning that\n43:      * the next fetch call should just resume from where the last fetch call was waken up or\n44:      * interrupted. It is up to the implementer to either read all the records of the split or to\n45:      * stop reading them at some point (for example when a given threshold is exceeded). In that\n46:      * later case, when fetch is called again, the reading should restart at the record where it\n47:      * left off based on the {@code SplitState}.\n48:      *\n49:      * @return the Ids of the finished splits.\n50:      * @throws IOException when encountered IO errors, such as deserialization failures.\n51:      */\n52:     RecordsWithSplitIds<E> fetch() throws IOException;\n53: \n54:     /**\n55:      * Handle the split changes. This call should be non-blocking.\n56:      *\n57:      * <p>For the consistency of internal state in SourceReaderBase, if an invalid split is added to\n58:      * the reader (for example splits without any records), it should be put back into {@link\n59:      * RecordsWithSplitIds} as finished splits so that SourceReaderBase could be able to clean up\n60:      * resources created for it.\n61:      *\n62:      * <p>For the consistency of internal state in SourceReaderBase, if a split is removed, it\n63:      * should be put back into {@link RecordsWithSplitIds} as finished splits so that\n64:      * SourceReaderBase could be able to clean up resources created for it.\n65:      *\n66:      * @param splitsChanges the split changes that the SplitReader needs to handle.\n67:      */\n68:     void handleSplitsChanges(SplitsChange<SplitT> splitsChanges);\n69: \n70:     /** Wake up the split reader in case the fetcher thread is blocking in {@link #fetch()}. */\n71:     void wakeUp();\n72: \n73:     /**\n74:      * Pauses or resumes reading of individual splits readers.\n75:      *\n76:      * <p>Note that no other methods can be called in parallel, so it's fine to non-atomically\n77:      * update subscriptions. This method is simply providing connectors with more expressive APIs\n78:      * the opportunity to update all subscriptions at once.\n79:      *\n80:      * <p>This is currently used to align the watermarks of splits, if watermark alignment is used\n81:      * and the source reads from more than one split.\n82:      *\n83:      * <p>The default implementation throws an {@link UnsupportedOperationException} where the\n84:      * default implementation will be removed in future releases. To be compatible with future\n85:      * releases, it is recommended to implement this method and override the default implementation.\n86:      *\n87:      * @param splitsToPause the splits to pause\n88:      * @param splitsToResume the splits to resume\n89:      */\n90:     default void pauseOrResumeSplits(\n91:             Collection<SplitT> splitsToPause, Collection<SplitT> splitsToResume) {\n92:         throw new UnsupportedOperationException(\n93:                 \"This split reader does not support pausing or resuming splits which can lead to unaligned splits.\\n\"\n94:                         + \"Unaligned splits are splits where the output watermarks of the splits have diverged more than the allowed limit.\\n\"\n95:                         + \"It is highly discouraged to use unaligned source splits, as this leads to unpredictable\\n\"\n96:                         + \"watermark alignment if there is more than a single split per reader. It is recommended to implement pausing splits\\n\"\n97:                         + \"for this source. At your own risk, you can allow unaligned source splits by setting the\\n\"\n98:                         + \"configuration parameter `pipeline.watermark-alignment.allow-unaligned-source-splits' to true.\\n\"\n99:                         + \"Beware that this configuration parameter will be dropped in a future Flink release.\");\n100:     }\n101: }\n102: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/flink--0cc95fcc@de39c3e1777c43fe3363b3fd7784bf46b57a99c2/-/blob/flink-connectors/flink-connector-base/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/connector/base/source/reader/splitreader/SplitReader.java"}}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01N97wYug6MuvQtfiqMyET7H","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01CwJdKUUCU67sAaHHdnQgmv","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/solution.md","content":"# Kafka-Flink Streaming Data Flow Architecture: Cross-Repository Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n\n### Apache Kafka (github.com/sg-benchmarks/kafka--0753c489)\n\n**Producer API:**\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/Producer.java` — Core interface defining send(), flush(), close() contracts for publishing to Kafka\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/ProducerRecord.java` — Immutable container for a (topic, partition, key, value) tuple sent to the broker\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/Callback.java` — Callback interface for async send completion\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/serialization/Serializer.java` — Generic serialization interface (configure(), serialize(topic, headers, data))\n\n**Consumer API:**\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/Consumer.java` — Core interface defining poll(), subscribe(), commitSync(), commitAsync(), seek() contracts\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/ConsumerRecord.java` — Immutable record read from Kafka with topic, partition, offset, timestamp, key, value, headers\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/OffsetAndMetadata.java` — Offset + optional metadata for commit state; includes leaderEpoch for log truncation detection\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/serialization/Deserializer.java` — Generic deserialization interface (configure(), deserialize(topic, headers, data))\n\n### Apache Flink (github.com/sg-benchmarks/flink--0cc95fcc)\n\n**Core Source API (flink-core module):**\n- `flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/connector/source/Source.java` — Factory interface that creates SourceReader (pull-based) and SplitEnumerator (coordinator-side); declares Boundedness\n- `flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/connector/source/SourceReader.java` — Pull-based interface: start(), pollNext(ReaderOutput), addSplits(), snapshotState(checkpointId)\n- `flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/connector/source/SourceSplit.java` — Interface for split metadata (represents a partition-like unit of work)\n- `flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/connector/source/SplitEnumerator.java` — Coordinator-side split discovery and assignment; snapshotState() for durability\n- `flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/connector/source/SourceReaderContext.java` — Runtime context providing sendSplitRequest(), sendSourceEventToCoordinator()\n- `flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/connector/source/ReaderOutput.java` — Sink for SourceReader to emit records and watermarks\n\n**Connector-Base Framework (flink-connectors/flink-connector-base):**\n- `flink-connectors/flink-connector-base/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/connector/base/source/reader/SourceReaderBase.java` — Reusable implementation of SourceReader with FutureCompletingBlockingQueue, SplitFetcherManager, RecordEmitter integration\n- `flink-connectors/flink-connector-base/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/connector/base/source/reader/splitreader/SplitReader.java` — Pluggable interface for split-specific I/O (fetch(), handleSplitsChanges(), wakeUp())\n- `flink-connectors/flink-connector-base/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/connector/base/source/reader/RecordEmitter.java` — Processes intermediate elements from SplitReader (E) and emits final elements (T) to SourceOutput\n\n**Runtime Integration (flink-runtime):**\n- `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/operators/SourceOperator.java` — StreamOperator that executes SourceReader; implements checkpoint integration via snapshotState() and notifyCheckpointComplete()\n- `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/runtime/tasks/SourceOperatorStreamTask.java` — StreamTask wrapper for SourceOperator with lifecycle management\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### 1. Kafka Producer Data Flow\n\n```\nUser Code\n    ↓\nProducerRecord<K, V> (topic, partition, key, value, headers, timestamp)\n    ↓\nProducer.send(record, callback)  ← Callback for async notification\n    ↓\nKafkaProducer (internal)\n    ├─ Serializer<K>.serialize(topic, headers, key)  → byte[]\n    ├─ Serializer<V>.serialize(topic, headers, value) → byte[]\n    ├─ Partitioner.partition(topic, key, ...) → partition ID\n    └─ Send to broker partition\n```\n\n**Key Characteristics:**\n- Serializers are configured with topic name + isKey flag\n- Header support allows side-channel metadata\n- Callback enables async processing; ProducerRecord includes RecordMetadata on success\n- Partitioner can be custom (e.g., locality-aware, key-based)\n\n### 2. Kafka Consumer Data Flow\n\n```\nKafkaConsumer\n    ↓\npoll(duration) ← Called in Flink loop\n    ↓\nFetcher (internal) — Manages TCP connections, deserialization, offset tracking\n    ├─ Pull ConsumerRecord batches from brokers\n    ├─ Deserializer<K>.deserialize(topic, headers, bytes) → key\n    ├─ Deserializer<V>.deserialize(topic, headers, bytes) → value\n    └─ Yields ConsumerRecord<K, V>(topic, partition, offset, timestamp, key, value, headers)\n    ↓\nConsumerRecords<K, V> (batch)\n    ↓\nApplication processes records\n    ↓\ncommitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)\n    ├─ OffsetAndMetadata { offset: long, metadata: String, leaderEpoch: Optional<Integer> }\n    └─ Updates __consumer_offsets topic; returns on success or throws CommitFailedException\n\ncommitAsync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>, OffsetCommitCallback)\n    └─ Callback notifies on success/failure asynchronously\n```\n\n**Key Characteristics:**\n- Consumer group coordination handles rebalancing via ConsumerRebalanceListener\n- Offset commits are idempotent; can be manual (commitSync/commitAsync) or automatic\n- LeaderEpoch in OffsetAndMetadata enables detection of log truncation\n- Deserializers have access to full ConsumerRecord headers and topic context\n\n### 3. Flink Source API Data Flow\n\n```\nSource<T, SplitT, EnumChkT> (Factory)\n    ├─ createEnumerator(context) → SplitEnumerator<SplitT, EnumChkT>\n    ├─ createReader(context) → SourceReader<T, SplitT>\n    ├─ getSplitSerializer() → SimpleVersionedSerializer<SplitT>\n    └─ getEnumeratorCheckpointSerializer() → SimpleVersionedSerializer<EnumChkT>\n\n    ↓\n\nSplitEnumerator (Coordinator, JobManager-side)\n    ├─ start()\n    ├─ addReader(subtaskId)\n    ├─ handleSplitRequest(subtaskId, hostname)\n    ├─ addSplitsBack(splits, subtaskId)  ← On reader failure\n    ├─ snapshotState(checkpointId) → EnumChkT\n    └─ handleSourceEvent(subtaskId, SourceEvent) ← Custom coordination\n\n    ↓ (SplitEnumeratorContext.assignSplit() / assignSplits())\n\nSourceReader (TaskManager-side, per parallel subtask)\n    ├─ start()\n    ├─ pollNext(ReaderOutput<T>) → InputStatus (MORE_AVAILABLE | NOTHING_AVAILABLE | END_OF_INPUT)\n    ├─ addSplits(List<SplitT>)\n    ├─ snapshotState(checkpointId) → List<SplitT>  ← Current splits + position within splits\n    ├─ notifyNoMoreSplits()\n    ├─ handleSourceEvents(SourceEvent)\n    └─ isAvailable() → CompletableFuture<Void>  ← Signals when data is available\n\n    ↓\n\nReaderOutput<T>\n    ├─ collect(record, timestamp)\n    ├─ collectWithTimestamp(record, timestamp)\n    └─ createOutputForSplit(splitId) → SourceOutput<T>\n```\n\n**Key Design Patterns:**\n- **FLIP-27 Split Model:** Partitions (Kafka partitions, file chunks, ranges) become \"Splits\"\n- **Pull-based Consumption:** SourceReader.pollNext() is synchronous, non-blocking; runtime polls in a loop\n- **Availability Signaling:** isAvailable() prevents busy-waiting when no data is ready\n- **Stateful Splits:** SourceReader.snapshotState() returns current split list (Flink manages offset state within splits via SourceReader implementation)\n\n### 4. Flink Connector-Base Framework\n\n**High-Level Architecture:**\n\n```\nSourceReaderBase<E, T, SplitT, SplitStateT> (Abstract)\n    │\n    ├─ SplitFetcherManager<E, SplitT>\n    │  └─ Manages pool of SplitFetcher threads\n    │     └─ Each fetcher owns a SplitReader<E, SplitT> and calls fetch() in a loop\n    │        └─ SplitReader interface is connector-specific:\n    │           - fetch() → RecordsWithSplitIds<E>\n    │           - handleSplitsChanges(SplitsChange<SplitT>)\n    │           - wakeUp()\n    │           - pauseOrResumeSplits(pause, resume)\n    │\n    ├─ RecordEmitter<E, T, SplitStateT> (User-provided)\n    │  └─ emitRecord(E element, SourceOutput<T> output, SplitStateT splitState)\n    │     └─ Transforms intermediate type E (from SplitReader.fetch()) → final type T (downstream)\n    │     └─ Updates mutable split state (e.g., offsets, positions)\n    │\n    ├─ FutureCompletingBlockingQueue<RecordsWithSplitIds<E>>\n    │  └─ Hand-over queue between fetcher threads and main task thread\n    │  └─ Supports backpressure via blocking semantics\n    │\n    └─ pollNext(ReaderOutput<T>)\n       ├─ Dequeue RecordsWithSplitIds<E> from queue\n       ├─ For each element E:\n       │  ├─ Look up SplitContext<T, SplitStateT> for the split\n       │  ├─ Call recordEmitter.emitRecord(E, output, splitState)\n       │  ├─ Split state mutation enables position tracking\n       │  └─ Emit to SourceOutput<T>\n       ├─ Return InputStatus based on queue availability\n       └─ On error, exception in SplitReader triggers split reassignment\n```\n\n**Key Design Principles:**\n- **Thread Separation:** SplitReader runs in fetcher threads; RecordEmitter/state updates in main task thread\n- **Backpressure Handling:** Blocking queue naturally slows fetchers when downstream is slow\n- **Split State Management:** User implements RecordEmitter to track state (e.g., Kafka offsets); snapshotState() returns split snapshot\n- **Pluggable SplitReader:** Each connector (Kafka, File, Custom) implements SplitReader for its I/O model\n\n**Integration with Kafka (Flink Kafka Connector Pattern):**\n\n```\nSource (Kafka)\n    ├─ createEnumerator()\n    │  └─ KafkaSourceEnumerator: Discovers partition list from broker metadata\n    │     └─ assignSplit(TopicPartition partition) to readers\n    │\n    └─ createReader()\n       └─ KafkaSourceReader extends SourceReaderBase\n          ├─ SplitFetcherManager with KafkaSplitReader\n          │  └─ KafkaSplitReader extends SplitReader<ConsumerRecord, KafkaPartitionSplit>\n          │     ├─ Creates KafkaConsumer (one per fetcher thread)\n          │     ├─ fetch() → Calls consumer.poll(), deserializes records\n          │     └─ handleSplitsChanges() → Adjusts subscriptions\n          │\n          └─ KafkaRecordEmitter extends RecordEmitter<ConsumerRecord, T, KafkaPartitionState>\n             ├─ emitRecord(ConsumerRecord, output, state)\n             │  ├─ Apply user DeserializationSchema (Flink layer) on value\n             │  ├─ Extract timestamp, watermark\n             │  └─ Update state.currentOffset to record.offset()\n             └─ snapshotState() returns List<KafkaPartitionSplit> with latest offsets\n```\n\n### 5. Serialization/Deserialization Boundary\n\n**Dual Serialization Layers:**\n\n```\nExternal Kafka Broker Storage (wire format)\n    ↑↓ (Kafka Serializer/Deserializer)\nKafka ConsumerRecord (bytes) / ProducerRecord (bytes)\n    │\n    │ Flink SourceReader/Sink wraps ConsumerRecord\n    │\nFlink DeserializationSchema / SerializationSchema (user-provided)\n    ↓\nJava Typed Objects (T)\n    ↓\nFlink StreamRecord<T>\n    ↓\nDownstream Operators\n```\n\n**Schema Interfaces in Flink:**\n\n```java\n// Flink deser/ser (declarative format description)\npublic interface DeserializationSchema<T> {\n    T deserialize(byte[] data) throws IOException;\n    TypeInformation<T> getProducedType();\n}\n\npublic interface SerializationSchema<T> {\n    byte[] serialize(T element);\n}\n```\n\n**Why Two Layers?**\n\n1. **Kafka Serializer/Deserializer:**\n   - Native to Kafka; configured per topic\n   - Topic-aware: receives topic name, can branch logic\n   - Optional headers support for metadata\n   - Examples: StringSerializer, JsonSerializer, AvroSerializer\n\n2. **Flink DeserializationSchema:**\n   - Higher-level wrapper for Kafka values only (not keys)\n   - Provides TypeInformation (Flink's type system)\n   - Decouples user data transformation from Kafka's envelope\n   - Examples: JsonDeserializationSchema<T>, AvroDeserializationSchema<T>\n\n**Integration Point:**\n```\nKafkaSplitReader.fetch()\n    ├─ consumer.poll() → ConsumerRecord<byte[], byte[]>\n    ├─ Kafka Deserializer<V>.deserialize(topic, headers, valuBytes) → V (intermediate type)\n    ├─ (Optional) Apply Flink DeserializationSchema<T> on V → T (final type)\n    └─ Wrap in RecordsWithSplitIds<ConsumerRecord<byte[], T>> for SourceReaderBase\n```\n\n---\n\n## Analysis: Checkpoint-Offset Integration\n\n### Flink Checkpoint Mechanism\n\n**Checkpoint Flow:**\n\n1. **Trigger Phase (JobManager):**\n   - JobManager sends checkpoint trigger to all operators\n   - Barriers are injected into stream\n\n2. **Snapshot Phase (SourceOperator):**\n   ```java\n   // SourceOperator.snapshotState(StateSnapshotContext context)\n   @Override\n   public void snapshotState(StateSnapshotContext context) throws Exception {\n       long checkpointId = context.getCheckpointId();\n       readerState.update(sourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId));\n   }\n   ```\n   - SourceOperator calls SourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId)\n   - SourceReader returns List<SplitT> (current splits with embedded state)\n   - State is stored in OperatorStateStore (ListState<SplitT>)\n\n3. **Commit Phase (after all operators snapshot):**\n   ```java\n   // SourceOperator.notifyCheckpointComplete(long checkpointId)\n   @Override\n   public void notifyCheckpointComplete(long checkpointId) throws Exception {\n       sourceReader.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId);\n   }\n   ```\n   - SourceReader.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId) is called\n   - **This is where Kafka offset commits happen**\n\n### Kafka Integration Point\n\n**In KafkaSourceReader (extending SourceReaderBase):**\n\n```\nSourceReaderBase.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)\n    └─ recordEmitter.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)  [if supported]\n\nOR (direct in SourceReader subclass):\n\n    └─ For each KafkaPartitionState in snapshotState():\n       ├─ Extract lastSuccessfulOffset\n       ├─ Create OffsetAndMetadata(lastSuccessfulOffset, metadata=\"checkpoint-123\")\n       ├─ Call kafkaConsumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)\n       └─ Blocks until __consumer_offsets topic is updated\n```\n\n**Why This Works:**\n\n1. **Exactly-Once Semantics:**\n   - Flink checkpoint is taken atomically across all operators\n   - Only after ALL operators (including downstream sinks) successfully snapshot\n   - Kafka offset is committed within the same checkpoint boundary\n   - If job fails mid-checkpoint, offsets are NOT committed; replay from last checkpoint\n\n2. **Dual Commit Log:**\n   - Flink state: OperatorStateStore (task-side state snapshot)\n   - Kafka state: __consumer_offsets topic (consumer group offset commit)\n   - On recovery, Flink reads its state to restore SourceReader.snapshotState()\n   - SourceReader calls addSplits(splits) with the restored offsets\n   - Kafka consumer seeks to those offsets and resumes\n\n3. **Offset Deduplication:**\n   - Checkpoints are idempotent in Kafka (duplicate commits with same offset are no-ops)\n   - If Flink retries a checkpoint, committing same offset again is safe\n   - Consumer group metadata in OffsetAndMetadata can track which checkpoint was committed\n\n### Thread Architecture\n\n**Flink Task Thread (Main):**\n```\nStreamTask.run()\n    └─ SourceOperator.emitNext(DataOutput)\n       ├─ sourceReader.pollNext(output)\n       │  └─ Block until data available (via isAvailable() future)\n       └─ Emit records downstream in batch or individual\n```\n\n**Kafka Fetcher Threads (In KafkaConsumer):**\n```\nKafkaConsumer (internal Fetcher + Sender threads)\n    ├─ Fetcher thread:\n    │  ├─ Periodically fetch from brokers\n    │  ├─ Deserialize with Kafka Deserializer\n    │  └─ Buffer in internal queue (auto.offset.reset logic)\n    │\n    └─ Sender thread:\n       ├─ Batch offsets for commit\n       ├─ On notifyCheckpointComplete():\n       │  └─ commitSync() blocks until broker acks\n       └─ Can be overridden to use commitAsync() with callback\n```\n\n**Synchronization:**\n- SourceReaderBase uses FutureCompletingBlockingQueue for hand-over\n- SplitFetcher thread calls fetch() in loop, enqueues RecordsWithSplitIds\n- Main task thread dequeues, calls recordEmitter.emitRecord()\n- Main thread handles checkpoints; notifyCheckpointComplete() is called sequentially\n- Kafka offset commit is blocking (commitSync) in notifyCheckpointComplete context\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kafka-Flink integration exemplifies a clean architectural separation of concerns across two independent systems:\n\n**Kafka's Role:** Provides the persistent event log (topics) with partition-granular consumption via KafkaConsumer, offset management through __consumer_offsets topic, and serialization SPI (Serializer/Deserializer) for value transformation.\n\n**Flink's Role:** Abstracts Kafka's consumer as a Source (pull-based SourceReader), maps partitions to Splits, orchestrates distributed consumption via SplitEnumerator coordination, and integrates offset state into Flink's checkpoint mechanism for exactly-once semantics.\n\n**The Bridge:** The Flink Kafka Connector implements:\n- KafkaSplitReader (wraps KafkaConsumer.poll() into fetch())\n- KafkaRecordEmitter (applies DeserializationSchema, tracks offsets in split state)\n- KafkaSourceReader extends SourceReaderBase (manages multiple fetcher threads, FutureCompletingBlockingQueue for backpressure)\n- Upon checkpoint completion, offsets are committed to Kafka via commitSync(), ensuring durable offset tracking aligned with Flink's state backend\n\nThis architecture enables:\n- **Exactly-once delivery**: Checkpoints encapsulate both Flink state and Kafka offsets\n- **Backpressure**: Blocking queue and isAvailable() signaling prevent unbounded buffering\n- **Scalability**: Splits assigned dynamically; SplitEnumerator discovers partitions, SourceReaders consume in parallel\n- **Flexibility**: Custom SplitReader, RecordEmitter, and DeserializationSchema allow connector-specific optimization (batching, local I/O, custom state)\n\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":577,"cache_read_input_tokens":121470,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":577},"output_tokens":2,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"f88f8b8d-c080-4510-a5ce-bae3838faaef","uuid":"74d78294-c018-4afc-89ca-31dbbd2503e2"}

includes leaderEpoch for log truncation detection\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/serialization/Deserializer.java` — Generic deserialization interface (configure(), deserialize(topic, headers, data))\n\n### Apache Flink (github.com/sg-benchmarks/flink--0cc95fcc)\n\n**Core Source API (flink-core module):**\n- `flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/connector/source/Source.java` — Factory interface that creates SourceReader (pull-based) and SplitEnumerator (coordinator-side); declares Boundedness\n- `flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/connector/source/SourceReader.java` — Pull-based interface: start(), pollNext(ReaderOutput), addSplits(), snapshotState(checkpointId)\n- `flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/connector/source/SourceSplit.java` — Interface for split metadata (represents a partition-like unit of work)\n- `flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/connector/source/SplitEnumerator.java` — Coordinator-side split discovery and assignment; snapshotState() for durability\n- `flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/connector/source/SourceReaderContext.java` — Runtime context providing sendSplitRequest(), sendSourceEventToCoordinator()\n- `flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/connector/source/ReaderOutput.java` — Sink for SourceReader to emit records and watermarks\n\n**Connector-Base Framework (flink-connectors/flink-connector-base):**\n- `flink-connectors/flink-connector-base/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/connector/base/source/reader/SourceReaderBase.java` — Reusable implementation of SourceReader with FutureCompletingBlockingQueue, SplitFetcherManager, RecordEmitter integration\n- `flink-connectors/flink-connector-base/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/connector/base/source/reader/splitreader/SplitReader.java` — Pluggable interface for split-specific I/O (fetch(), handleSplitsChanges(), wakeUp())\n- `flink-connectors/flink-connector-base/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/connector/base/source/reader/RecordEmitter.java` — Processes intermediate elements from SplitReader (E) and emits final elements (T) to SourceOutput\n\n**Runtime Integration (flink-runtime):**\n- `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/operators/SourceOperator.java` — StreamOperator that executes SourceReader; implements checkpoint integration via snapshotState() and notifyCheckpointComplete()\n- `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/runtime/tasks/SourceOperatorStreamTask.java` — StreamTask wrapper for SourceOperator with lifecycle management\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### 1. Kafka Producer Data Flow\n\n```\nUser Code\n    ↓\nProducerRecord<K, V> (topic, partition, key, value, headers, timestamp)\n    ↓\nProducer.send(record, callback)  ← Callback for async notification\n    ↓\nKafkaProducer (internal)\n    ├─ Serializer<K>.serialize(topic, headers, key)  → byte[]\n    ├─ Serializer<V>.serialize(topic, headers, value) → byte[]\n    ├─ Partitioner.partition(topic, key, ...) → partition ID\n    └─ Send to broker partition\n```\n\n**Key Characteristics:**\n- Serializers are configured with topic name + isKey flag\n- Header support allows side-channel metadata\n- Callback enables async processing; ProducerRecord includes RecordMetadata on success\n- Partitioner can be custom (e.g., locality-aware, key-based)\n\n### 2. Kafka Consumer Data Flow\n\n```\nKafkaConsumer\n    ↓\npoll(duration) ← Called in Flink loop\n    ↓\nFetcher (internal) — Manages TCP connections, deserialization, offset tracking\n    ├─ Pull ConsumerRecord batches from brokers\n    ├─ Deserializer<K>.deserialize(topic, headers, bytes) → key\n    ├─ Deserializer<V>.deserialize(topic, headers, bytes) → value\n    └─ Yields ConsumerRecord<K, V>(topic, partition, offset, timestamp, key, value, headers)\n    ↓\nConsumerRecords<K, V> (batch)\n    ↓\nApplication processes records\n    ↓\ncommitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)\n    ├─ OffsetAndMetadata { offset: long, metadata: String, leaderEpoch: Optional<Integer> }\n    └─ Updates __consumer_offsets topic; returns on success or throws CommitFailedException\n\ncommitAsync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>, OffsetCommitCallback)\n    └─ Callback notifies on success/failure asynchronously\n```\n\n**Key Characteristics:**\n- Consumer group coordination handles rebalancing via ConsumerRebalanceListener\n- Offset commits are idempotent; can be manual (commitSync/commitAsync) or automatic\n- LeaderEpoch in OffsetAndMetadata enables detection of log truncation\n- Deserializers have access to full ConsumerRecord headers and topic context\n\n### 3. Flink Source API Data Flow\n\n```\nSource<T, SplitT, EnumChkT> (Factory)\n    ├─ createEnumerator(context) → SplitEnumerator<SplitT, EnumChkT>\n    ├─ createReader(context) → SourceReader<T, SplitT>\n    ├─ getSplitSerializer() → SimpleVersionedSerializer<SplitT>\n    └─ getEnumeratorCheckpointSerializer() → SimpleVersionedSerializer<EnumChkT>\n\n    ↓\n\nSplitEnumerator (Coordinator, JobManager-side)\n    ├─ start()\n    ├─ addReader(subtaskId)\n    ├─ handleSplitRequest(subtaskId, hostname)\n    ├─ addSplitsBack(splits, subtaskId)  ← On reader failure\n    ├─ snapshotState(checkpointId) → EnumChkT\n    └─ handleSourceEvent(subtaskId, SourceEvent) ← Custom coordination\n\n    ↓ (SplitEnumeratorContext.assignSplit() / assignSplits())\n\nSourceReader (TaskManager-side, per parallel subtask)\n    ├─ start()\n    ├─ pollNext(ReaderOutput<T>) → InputStatus (MORE_AVAILABLE | NOTHING_AVAILABLE | END_OF_INPUT)\n    ├─ addSplits(List<SplitT>)\n    ├─ snapshotState(checkpointId) → List<SplitT>  ← Current splits + position within splits\n    ├─ notifyNoMoreSplits()\n    ├─ handleSourceEvents(SourceEvent)\n    └─ isAvailable() → CompletableFuture<Void>  ← Signals when data is available\n\n    ↓\n\nReaderOutput<T>\n    ├─ collect(record, timestamp)\n    ├─ collectWithTimestamp(record, timestamp)\n    └─ createOutputForSplit(splitId) → SourceOutput<T>\n```\n\n**Key Design Patterns:**\n- **FLIP-27 Split Model:** Partitions (Kafka partitions, file chunks, ranges) become \"Splits\"\n- **Pull-based Consumption:** SourceReader.pollNext() is synchronous, non-blocking; runtime polls in a loop\n- **Availability Signaling:** isAvailable() prevents busy-waiting when no data is ready\n- **Stateful Splits:** SourceReader.snapshotState() returns current split list (Flink manages offset state within splits via SourceReader implementation)\n\n### 4. Flink Connector-Base Framework\n\n**High-Level Architecture:**\n\n```\nSourceReaderBase<E, T, SplitT, SplitStateT> (Abstract)\n    │\n    ├─ SplitFetcherManager<E, SplitT>\n    │  └─ Manages pool of SplitFetcher threads\n    │     └─ Each fetcher owns a SplitReader<E, SplitT> and calls fetch() in a loop\n    │        └─ SplitReader interface is connector-specific:\n    │           - fetch() → RecordsWithSplitIds<E>\n    │           - handleSplitsChanges(SplitsChange<SplitT>)\n    │           - wakeUp()\n    │           - pauseOrResumeSplits(pause, resume)\n    │\n    ├─ RecordEmitter<E, T, SplitStateT> (User-provided)\n    │  └─ emitRecord(E element, SourceOutput<T> output, SplitStateT splitState)\n    │     └─ Transforms intermediate type E (from SplitReader.fetch()) → final type T (downstream)\n    │     └─ Updates mutable split state (e.g., offsets, positions)\n    │\n    ├─ FutureCompletingBlockingQueue<RecordsWithSplitIds<E>>\n    │  └─ Hand-over queue between fetcher threads and main task thread\n    │  └─ Supports backpressure via blocking semantics\n    │\n    └─ pollNext(ReaderOutput<T>)\n       ├─ Dequeue RecordsWithSplitIds<E> from queue\n       ├─ For each element E:\n       │  ├─ Look up SplitContext<T, SplitStateT> for the split\n       │  ├─ Call recordEmitter.emitRecord(E, output, splitState)\n       │  ├─ Split state mutation enables position tracking\n       │  └─ Emit to SourceOutput<T>\n       ├─ Return InputStatus based on queue availability\n       └─ On error, exception in SplitReader triggers split reassignment\n```\n\n**Key Design Principles:**\n- **Thread Separation:** SplitReader runs in fetcher threads; RecordEmitter/state updates in main task thread\n- **Backpressure Handling:** Blocking queue naturally slows fetchers when downstream is slow\n- **Split State Management:** User implements RecordEmitter to track state (e.g., Kafka offsets); snapshotState() returns split snapshot\n- **Pluggable SplitReader:** Each connector (Kafka, File, Custom) implements SplitReader for its I/O model\n\n**Integration with Kafka (Flink Kafka Connector Pattern):**\n\n```\nSource (Kafka)\n    ├─ createEnumerator()\n    │  └─ KafkaSourceEnumerator: Discovers partition list from broker metadata\n    │     └─ assignSplit(TopicPartition partition) to readers\n    │\n    └─ createReader()\n       └─ KafkaSourceReader extends SourceReaderBase\n          ├─ SplitFetcherManager with KafkaSplitReader\n          │  └─ KafkaSplitReader extends SplitReader<ConsumerRecord, KafkaPartitionSplit>\n          │     ├─ Creates KafkaConsumer (one per fetcher thread)\n          │     ├─ fetch() → Calls consumer.poll(), deserializes records\n          │     └─ handleSplitsChanges() → Adjusts subscriptions\n          │\n          └─ KafkaRecordEmitter extends RecordEmitter<ConsumerRecord, T, KafkaPartitionState>\n             ├─ emitRecord(ConsumerRecord, output, state)\n             │  ├─ Apply user DeserializationSchema (Flink layer) on value\n             │  ├─ Extract timestamp, watermark\n             │  └─ Update state.currentOffset to record.offset()\n             └─ snapshotState() returns List<KafkaPartitionSplit> with latest offsets\n```\n\n### 5. Serialization/Deserialization Boundary\n\n**Dual Serialization Layers:**\n\n```\nExternal Kafka Broker Storage (wire format)\n    ↑↓ (Kafka Serializer/Deserializer)\nKafka ConsumerRecord (bytes) / ProducerRecord (bytes)\n    │\n    │ Flink SourceReader/Sink wraps ConsumerRecord\n    │\nFlink DeserializationSchema / SerializationSchema (user-provided)\n    ↓\nJava Typed Objects (T)\n    ↓\nFlink StreamRecord<T>\n    ↓\nDownstream Operators\n```\n\n**Schema Interfaces in Flink:**\n\n```java\n// Flink deser/ser (declarative format description)\npublic interface DeserializationSchema<T> {\n    T deserialize(byte[] data) throws IOException;\n    TypeInformation<T> getProducedType();\n}\n\npublic interface SerializationSchema<T> {\n    byte[] serialize(T element);\n}\n```\n\n**Why Two Layers?**\n\n1. **Kafka Serializer/Deserializer:**\n   - Native to Kafka; configured per topic\n   - Topic-aware: receives topic name, can branch logic\n   - Optional headers support for metadata\n   - Examples: StringSerializer, JsonSerializer, AvroSerializer\n\n2. **Flink DeserializationSchema:**\n   - Higher-level wrapper for Kafka values only (not keys)\n   - Provides TypeInformation (Flink's type system)\n   - Decouples user data transformation from Kafka's envelope\n   - Examples: JsonDeserializationSchema<T>, AvroDeserializationSchema<T>\n\n**Integration Point:**\n```\nKafkaSplitReader.fetch()\n    ├─ consumer.poll() → ConsumerRecord<byte[], byte[]>\n    ├─ Kafka Deserializer<V>.deserialize(topic, headers, valuBytes) → V (intermediate type)\n    ├─ (Optional) Apply Flink DeserializationSchema<T> on V → T (final type)\n    └─ Wrap in RecordsWithSplitIds<ConsumerRecord<byte[], T>> for SourceReaderBase\n```\n\n---\n\n## Analysis: Checkpoint-Offset Integration\n\n### Flink Checkpoint Mechanism\n\n**Checkpoint Flow:**\n\n1. **Trigger Phase (JobManager):**\n   - JobManager sends checkpoint trigger to all operators\n   - Barriers are injected into stream\n\n2. **Snapshot Phase (SourceOperator):**\n   ```java\n   // SourceOperator.snapshotState(StateSnapshotContext context)\n   @Override\n   public void snapshotState(StateSnapshotContext context) throws Exception {\n       long checkpointId = context.getCheckpointId();\n       readerState.update(sourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId));\n   }\n   ```\n   - SourceOperator calls SourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId)\n   - SourceReader returns List<SplitT> (current splits with embedded state)\n   - State is stored in OperatorStateStore (ListState<SplitT>)\n\n3. **Commit Phase (after all operators snapshot):**\n   ```java\n   // SourceOperator.notifyCheckpointComplete(long checkpointId)\n   @Override\n   public void notifyCheckpointComplete(long checkpointId) throws Exception {\n       sourceReader.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId);\n   }\n   ```\n   - SourceReader.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId) is called\n   - **This is where Kafka offset commits happen**\n\n### Kafka Integration Point\n\n**In KafkaSourceReader (extending SourceReaderBase):**\n\n```\nSourceReaderBase.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)\n    └─ recordEmitter.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)  [if supported]\n\nOR (direct in SourceReader subclass):\n\n    └─ For each KafkaPartitionState in snapshotState():\n       ├─ Extract lastSuccessfulOffset\n       ├─ Create OffsetAndMetadata(lastSuccessfulOffset, metadata=\"checkpoint-123\")\n       ├─ Call kafkaConsumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)\n       └─ Blocks until __consumer_offsets topic is updated\n```\n\n**Why This Works:**\n\n1. **Exactly-Once Semantics:**\n   - Flink checkpoint is taken atomically across all operators\n   - Only after ALL operators (including downstream sinks) successfully snapshot\n   - Kafka offset is committed within the same checkpoint boundary\n   - If job fails mid-checkpoint, offsets are NOT committed; replay from last checkpoint\n\n2. **Dual Commit Log:**\n   - Flink state: OperatorStateStore (task-side state snapshot)\n   - Kafka state: __consumer_offsets topic (consumer group offset commit)\n   - On recovery, Flink reads its state to restore SourceReader.snapshotState()\n   - SourceReader calls addSplits(splits) with the restored offsets\n   - Kafka consumer seeks to those offsets and resumes\n\n3. **Offset Deduplication:**\n   - Checkpoints are idempotent in Kafka (duplicate commits with same offset are no-ops)\n   - If Flink retries a checkpoint, committing same offset again is safe\n   - Consumer group metadata in OffsetAndMetadata can track which checkpoint was committed\n\n### Thread Architecture\n\n**Flink Task Thread (Main):**\n```\nStreamTask.run()\n    └─ SourceOperator.emitNext(DataOutput)\n       ├─ sourceReader.pollNext(output)\n       │  └─ Block until data available (via isAvailable() future)\n       └─ Emit records downstream in batch or individual\n```\n\n**Kafka Fetcher Threads (In KafkaConsumer):**\n```\nKafkaConsumer (internal Fetcher + Sender threads)\n    ├─ Fetcher thread:\n    │  ├─ Periodically fetch from brokers\n    │  ├─ Deserialize with Kafka Deserializer\n    │  └─ Buffer in internal queue (auto.offset.reset logic)\n    │\n    └─ Sender thread:\n       ├─ Batch offsets for commit\n       ├─ On notifyCheckpointComplete():\n       │  └─ commitSync() blocks until broker acks\n       └─ Can be overridden to use commitAsync() with callback\n```\n\n**Synchronization:**\n- SourceReaderBase uses FutureCompletingBlockingQueue for hand-over\n- SplitFetcher thread calls fetch() in loop, enqueues RecordsWithSplitIds\n- Main task thread dequeues, calls recordEmitter.emitRecord()\n- Main thread handles checkpoints; notifyCheckpointComplete() is called sequentially\n- Kafka offset commit is blocking (commitSync) in notifyCheckpointComplete context\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kafka-Flink integration exemplifies a clean architectural separation of concerns across two independent systems:\n\n**Kafka's Role:** Provides the persistent event log (topics) with partition-granular consumption via KafkaConsumer, offset management through __consumer_offsets topic, and serialization SPI (Serializer/Deserializer) for value transformation.\n\n**Flink's Role:** Abstracts Kafka's consumer as a Source (pull-based SourceReader), maps partitions to Splits, orchestrates distributed consumption via SplitEnumerator coordination, and integrates offset state into Flink's checkpoint mechanism for exactly-once semantics.\n\n**The Bridge:** The Flink Kafka Connector implements:\n- KafkaSplitReader (wraps KafkaConsumer.poll() into fetch())\n- KafkaRecordEmitter (applies DeserializationSchema, tracks offsets in split state)\n- KafkaSourceReader extends SourceReaderBase (manages multiple fetcher threads, FutureCompletingBlockingQueue for backpressure)\n- Upon checkpoint completion, offsets are committed to Kafka via commitSync(), ensuring durable offset tracking aligned with Flink's state backend\n\nThis architecture enables:\n- **Exactly-once delivery**: Checkpoints encapsulate both Flink state and Kafka offsets\n- **Backpressure**: Blocking queue and isAvailable() signaling prevent unbounded buffering\n- **Scalability**: Splits assigned dynamically; SplitEnumerator discovers partitions, SourceReaders consume in parallel\n- **Flexibility**: Custom SplitReader, RecordEmitter, and DeserializationSchema allow connector-specific optimization (batching, local I/O, custom state)\n\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
